473

he idea 
---
or this book came to me in February 2010 as I was running
along an empty Maine road be
---
ore sunrise and 
---
reezing my butt o
---

---

(or the small bony part o
---
 my anatomy that I call a “butt”).

The kernel o
---
that early morning brainstorm was to create the de
---
initive
list o
---
 the core tools you need to build 
---
urniture — no more, no less. I wanted

to help beginning woodworkers 
---
ocus only on those 40-odd tools, instead
o
---
 being distracted by the dozens and dozens o
---
 tools that look deceivingly
use
---
ul, but are really just nice reproductions o
---
 wildly unsuccess
---
ul tools that

collectors desired 
---
or their trophy rooms.
In short, I wanted to write the book that I wish I’d owned at age 11.

A
---
ter my run that February morning, I 
---
lopped on my bed and started
writing this book’s chapter on handplanes. When I 
---
inished it three days
later, I kinda liked it. I thought my employer would like it, too. So I wrote up
a 
---
ull proposal 
---
or this book and submitted it to my superiors at F+W Media.
About a week later my boss, Steve, sat down with me to discuss it.
While he liked my proposal, Steve thought it would be a better book i
---

I switched gears and 
---
ocused on blending hand and power tools instead o
---

my idea, which was to distill a list o
---
 the hard-core handtools, discuss how to

pick them then build a chest to protect them.
Steve argued that a book on blending hand and power tools would cast a

wider net and appeal to lots more woodworkers.
He's totally and completely correct.

But someone

else can write that

book.
I told Steve that I wouldn’t write the “blended woodworking” book he
wanted. While other bosses would have 
---
ired me 
---
or re
---
using, Steve has always given mea healthy length o
---
 rope.

So I dove into this book on my own time, and I latched onto the idea o
---

tying together the radical act o
---
 building 
---
urniture that lasts 
---
orever with
at
American anarchism, about which I knew just enough to be annoying
dinner parties.

474

THE

ANARCHIST’S

TOOL

CHEST

To augment my knowledge o
---
 American anarchism, I read a lot o
---
 books
with titles that alarmed both my liberal and conservative 
---
riends. I gathered

---
irst-hand accounts o
---
 pre-capitalistic artisans in Estonia and England. And
I became thoroughly convinced o
---
three things:

¢ We cannot look to our government to preserve woodworking. During

the last 20 years, our public school systems have only eliminated classes
in the manual arts. Our schools are designed to turn out machine-minders and computer nerds. There are no classes on how to be an “artisan.”
¢ We cannot look to 
---
ree enterprise to preserve woodworking. The last 100
years o
---
 mechanization have made most 
---
urniture and tools both cheap

and 
---
limsy. Corporations’ e
---

---
orts to make things cheaper and cheaper
only undermine good woodwork.

¢ The only people who will preserve our cra
---
t are the passionate amateurs,
who can pursue all manner o
---
 crazy historical methods without worrying
about starving.

Like it or not, these three points describe a typical buttoned-down, mildmannered American anarchist. That's me. And perhaps it’s you, too. You can

choose to call it “populism,” “pragmatism” or “mutualism.” But those are all
highbrow names 
---
or the 
---
ierce individualists who 
---
orged our young nation’s
pre-capitalistic society, which was based on the e
---

---
orts o
---
 millions o
---
 artisans
in wood, metal and cloth.

The deeper I delved into writing this book and the history o
---
 anarchism,

the more those long-dead artisans whispered the 
---
ollowing ideas into my ear:
Quit your corporate job. Get yoursel
---
 
---
ired.

But something keeps me on the payroll at Popular Woodworking Magazine.

Perhaps I’m just chicken. Or perhaps I still have work to do, and a corporation that turns out woodworking content 
---
or the masses is a great bullhorn

AFTERWORD

475


---
or my ideas on how to sustain our cra
---
t.
Someday my superiors will 
---
ind out that I’m hiding straight razors in the

bright red apples I hand out to readers o
---
 the magazine and my blogs. And
then I'll be back in business 
---
or mysel
---
 again. (I 
---
ailed miserably with a little

newspaper | helped launch in the mid-1990s.)
But until that day comes, let's just keep this little anarchism thing between you and me.

Date: Nov. 18, 2011
Shortly a
---
ter I wrote the 
---
inal paragraph (above) o
---
 my original text, I sent
the 
---
irst printing o
---
 this book to the presses. Then I had time to think — a
dangerous thing.

Some people (not me!) write books in hopes o
---
 changing the world. As a
li
---
elong writer I can tell you that what usually happens is that a book really

changes only one person — the author. A
---
ter 
---
orcing mysel
---
 to 
---
ace the stupid
things that institutions do to individuals, it became impossible 
---
or me to go

to work every day 
---
or one o
---
 these large institutions.
Lucky 
---
or me, my wi
---
e and I had paid o
---

---
 our mortgage in 2008. We had

no debts or obligations, other than our utilities and the cat 
---
ood bill. So I quit
my job. It was the happiest day o
---
 my li
---
e — right behind the birth o
---
 my two
children and my wedding day. (Right honey? Did I say that right?)
Since the day I walked out o
---
 my 
---
antastic dream job in June 2011 I have

---
ocused all my energy on publishing books and blog entries that promote the

cause o
---
 handwork — my true love.
By the time you read this, I might be handing you a carton o
---
 
---
ries via

some Midwestern drive-through window. But when I’m not cleaning out the
grease trap 
---
or the deep-
---
ryer or adjusting my hairnet to conceal my receeding hairline, I'll be writing outlines during my breaks 
---
or my next book.
Next up: Furniture design.
